<script>
  "use strict";

  var positionImage = function positionImage(imageEl) {
    var imageDimensions = imageEl.dataset.imageDimensions.split('x');
    var originalWidth = imageDimensions[0];
    var originalHeight = imageDimensions[1];
    var focalPoint = imageEl.dataset.imageFocalPoint.split(',');
    var focalPointX = focalPoint[0];
    var focalPointY = focalPoint[1];
    var parentNode = imageEl.parentNode;

    var scale = function () {
      var imageRatio = originalWidth / originalHeight;
      var parentClientSize = {
        height: parentNode.clientHeight,
        width: parentNode.clientWidth
      };
      var parentRatio = parentClientSize.width / parentClientSize.height;

      if (imageRatio > parentRatio) {
        return parentClientSize.height / originalHeight;
      }

      return parentClientSize.width / originalWidth;
    }();

    var getRelativeOffset = function getRelativeOffset() {
      var targetWidth = Math.ceil(originalWidth * scale);
      var targetHeight = Math.ceil(originalHeight * scale);
      var parentDimensionWidth = parentNode.offsetWidth;
      var parentDimensionHeight = parentNode.offsetHeight;
      var overflowWidth = targetWidth - parentDimensionWidth;
      var overflowHeight = targetHeight - parentDimensionHeight;
      var valueX;

      if (overflowWidth === 0) {
        valueX = focalPointX;
      } else {
        valueX = Math.max(Math.min(targetWidth * focalPointX - parentDimensionWidth * 0.5, overflowWidth), 0) / overflowWidth;
      }

      var valueY;

      if (overflowHeight === 0) {
        valueY = focalPointY;
      } else {
        valueY = Math.max(Math.min(targetHeight * focalPointY - parentDimensionHeight * 0.5, overflowHeight), 0) / overflowHeight;
      }

      return {
        valueX: valueX,
        valueY: valueY
      };
    };

    var relativeOffset = getRelativeOffset();
    var valueX = relativeOffset.valueX;
    var valueY = relativeOffset.valueY;
    imageEl.style.objectPosition = "".concat(valueX * 100, "% ").concat(valueY * 100, "%");
    Object.assign(imageEl.style, {
      height: '100%',
      width: '100%',
      objectFit: 'cover',
    });
  };
</script>

  



  
  
  <img alt=""
    
    data-src="https://images.squarespace-cdn.com/content/v1/60342fe77fcb2c03f66f4fa9/1614095005935-GOB5S4XQDDL534MSEWSJ/_MG_8204-1.jpg" data-image="https://images.squarespace-cdn.com/content/v1/60342fe77fcb2c03f66f4fa9/1614095005935-GOB5S4XQDDL534MSEWSJ/_MG_8204-1.jpg" data-image-dimensions="2500x1667" data-image-focal-point="0.5959040959040959,0.5200650081260157" alt="_MG_8204-1.jpg"

      onLoad="positionImage(this); this.classList.add('loaded');"
      loading="lazy"

            <div class="slide" data-type="image" data-animation-role="image">
              <div class="margin-wrapper">
                
                <a
                  
                    data-title=""
                    data-description="Staying in a bow-top wagon has always been a dream of mine. On my birthday at the start of the year my dream came true, thanks to Ben and his uncanny ability to filter through my constant inane rambling and pick out little nuggets of useful information 💙⁠⁣⁠
⁠⁣⁠
We spent two nights in this original restored bow-top gypsy wagon, complete with a wood-fire hot tub. The wagon was located in Appleby-in-Westmorland, the home of the annual Appleby Horse Fair, the largest gathering of Gypsies and Travellers in the UK. We soaked under the stars and the late Winter sunrise, and imagined what it would be like to roam the roads by horse and wagon.⁠⁣⁠
⁠⁣⁠
But it also got me thinking...⁠⁣⁠
⁠⁣⁠
It is a great shame that the United Kingdom has seen the steady decline and criminalisation of nomadic lifestyles over the last century, fuelled by land-grabbing and a belt of by-laws and restrictions that continues to be steadily tightened to this day. The UK operates on a culture of mistrust, of making rules for the many to compensate for the few. But by denying us the opportunity to connect with nature, how can we ever learn to respect her?⁠⁣⁠
⁣⁠
They have robbed us so gradually of our freedom to roam that we barely even noticed it happen, and placed us into restrictive little boxes earmarked by &amp;ldquo;No overnight parking&amp;rdquo; and &amp;ldquo;Private property&amp;rdquo; signs.⁣⁠
We have now lost touch with our nomadic roots to the point that we could scarcely find our way West without a compass, or know which wild plants are edible and which could kill us.⁣⁠
⁣⁠
It is a story that is echoed all over the world in which there is no longer a place for non-static, non-conforming peoples; after all, how can you tax those who do not pay for the land they live on? But where does that leave those of us with a destiny to wander?⁠⁣⁠
⁣⁠
I suppose it&amp;rsquo;s what drives us, personally, to seek ever-distant and freer lands. Countries that still allow you to wander and explore, that do not restrict but encourage our curiosity. ⁠
These are rare places, few and far between, and we strive to return this privilege of trust by respecting the sanctuary of nature we call home for the night.⁣"

            <div class="slide" data-type="image" data-animation-role="image">
              <div class="margin-wrapper">
                
                <a
                  
                    data-title=""
                    data-description="On this day we set out to fulfil one of my longstanding dreams; to see the house that was the inspiration for Emily Bront&amp;euml;&amp;rsquo;s Wuthering Heights. The image of the windswept building described in the novel had always stuck in my mind, and I wanted to see it for myself. ⁣⁣⁣⁠⁠
⁣⁣⁠⁠
Leaving the comfort of our rented shepherd's hut behind we set out on the 4 mile hike, and were treated to panoramic views of pristine moorland and wind-flattened grasses which swirled in umber colours not unlike a painting.⁣⁣⁠⁠
⁣⁣⁣⁠⁠
The remoteness of this farmhouse, in one of the most densely populated countries in Europe, was staggering. Situated next to a spring, and with plenty of wild pheasant about to shoot, eking out a meagre existence here would&amp;rsquo;ve nonetheless been a difficult task. A full day&amp;rsquo;s round trip to the nearest village where its residents could trade or sell, devoid of any roads, neighbours or arable land, it was both beautifully and damningly isolated. No wonder it now lay in ruin.⁣⁣⁣⁠⁠
⁣⁣⁣⁠⁠
That night we set up camp deep in the Yorkshire Dales by a river which undulated through a sheltered valley. The hills around us were tinted pale gold and the water rippled in lilac sunset hues, but we waited until almost dark to set up camp.⁣⁣⁣⁠⁠
⁣⁣⁣⁠⁠
Wild camping in the UK is a much trickier business than on the continent, due to almost every parcel of land being privately owned and attitudes towards campers generally being poor. In fact we&amp;rsquo;d not long set up our little campsite when a shiny Land Rover roared past, blaring its horn all the way down the road.⁣⁣⁠⁠
As the temperature dropped and the grass turned crunchy from frost, we hoped the angry driver would spare us in our thin nylon tent a thought as he relaxed in his warm, cozy house that evening. ⁣⁠⁠
⁣⁠⁠
The next day our bones were aching with cold, frozen from our nights&amp;rsquo; wild camp. So what better way to warm up than a pint by the fire at the Tan Hill Inn, the highest pub in Britain and a beacon for weary travellers.⁣⁠⁠
